ID: T15.G5.05
Topic: T15 – Stories & Animation
Skill: Join text strings
Description: Use `join [Hello ] (player name)` to create dynamic dialogue that incorporates variables, user input, or computed values into story text.

Dependencies:
* T15.G5.04: Layering logic
* T15.G4.05: Ask and Answer


ID: T15.G5.06
Topic: T15 – Stories & Animation
Skill: Text effects (Typewriter)
Description: Create a typewriter effect using a loop with `say (letter (i) of (text))` incrementing through each character with a short wait, revealing dialogue one letter at a time.

Dependencies:
* T15.G5.05: Join text strings
* T07.G3.01: Use a counted repeat loop


ID: T15.G5.07
Topic: T15 – Stories & Animation
Skill: Track story choices
Description: Use a variable like `(Trust)` or `(Karma)` to track cumulative player decisions throughout the story. Increment or decrement based on choices to influence later story events.

Dependencies:
* T15.G5.06: Text effects (Typewriter)
* T09.G3.01: Create and use a numeric variable for score or count


ID: T15.G5.08
Topic: T15 – Stories & Animation
Skill: Conditional endings
Description: Use `if <(Trust) > (5)> then switch backdrop to [Good Ending]` to show different endings based on accumulated player choices tracked in variables.

Dependencies:
* T15.G5.07: Track story choices
* T08.G3.01: Use a simple if in a script


ID: T15.G6.01
Topic: T15 – Stories & Animation
Skill: State Machine for Animation
Description: Use a `(State)` variable with values like "Idle", "Walk", "Talk" to control which animation loop plays. A forever loop checks the state and runs the appropriate costume animation sequence.

Dependencies:
* T15.G5.08: Conditional endings
* T09.G4.01: Use variables to track multiple states simultaneously


ID: T15.G6.02
Topic: T15 – Stories & Animation
Skill: List-based Dialogue
Description: Store dialogue lines in a list and use `repeat (length of [dialogue])` with `say (item (i) of [dialogue])` to iterate through them, making dialogue easy to edit and extend.

Dependencies:
* T15.G6.01: State Machine for Animation
* T10.G4.01: Use lists for dynamic data storage


ID: T15.G6.03
Topic: T15 – Stories & Animation
Skill: Cutscene controller
Description: Create a "Cutscene" custom block that uses `broadcast and wait` to sequence multiple character actions, ensuring each animation completes before the next begins.

Dependencies:
* T15.G6.02: List-based Dialogue
* T11.G4.01: Create custom blocks with inputs


ID: T15.G7.01
Topic: T15 – Stories & Animation
Skill: Scene Graph / Manager
Description: Create a dedicated "Manager" sprite that handles all broadcasts, tracks current scene in a variable, and coordinates global state changes (Scene 1 -> Scene 2) for the entire story.

Dependencies:
* T15.G6.03: Cutscene controller
* T15.G5.01: Broadcast scene change



ID: T15.G7.02
Topic: T15 – Stories & Animation
Skill: Lip Sync Logic
Description: Use `loudness` sensor or sound analysis to automatically switch between mouth-open and mouth-closed costumes, creating realistic lip sync for character dialogue.

Dependencies:
* T15.G7.01: Scene Graph / Manager
* T15.G4.02: Costume number logic



ID: T15.G7.03
Topic: T15 – Stories & Animation
Skill: Dialogue system with speaker tags
Description: Build a dialogue system where each list item contains speaker name and text (e.g., "Alice:Hello!"). Parse the string to show the correct sprite speaking with `item () of [split]` operations.

Dependencies:
* T15.G7.02: Lip Sync Logic
* T15.G6.02: List-based Dialogue


ID: T15.G8.01
Topic: T15 – Stories & Animation
Skill: Branching Narrative Engine
Description: Build a data-driven story engine using a table or list of lists where each row contains: node ID, dialogue text, choice options, and next node IDs. The engine reads and navigates this structure based on player choices.

Dependencies:
* T15.G7.03: Dialogue system with speaker tags
* T10.G6.01: Use nested lists or tables for structured data


ID: T15.G8.02
Topic: T15 – Stories & Animation
Skill: Accessibility in Media
Description: Implement accessibility features: use text-to-speech blocks for audio narration, display subtitle widgets synchronized with audio, and provide keyboard alternatives to mouse interactions.

Dependencies:
* T15.G8.01: Branching Narrative Engine
* T16.G7.03: Design an accessible interface for users with different abilities


ID: T15.G8.03
Topic: T15 – Stories & Animation
Skill: Save and load story progress
Description: Use cloud variables or local storage to save player progress (current scene, choices made, variables) so players can continue their story later. Implement load functionality to restore the saved state.

Dependencies:
* T15.G8.02: Accessibility in Media
* T09.G6.01: Use variables to represent real-world quantities


ID: T16.G3.01
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Add a button widget to the stage
Description: Use the "add button widget" block to create a clickable button on the stage. Specify the button's name, text label, and initial position (x, y coordinates). Understand that widgets are UI elements that float above sprites.

Dependencies:
* T06.G3.01: Build a green‑flag script that runs a 3–5 block sequence
* T01.G3.01: Complete a simple script with missing blocks


ID: T16.G3.02
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Handle a button click event
Description: Use the "when widget clicked" event block to run code when a button is clicked. Connect button clicks to simple actions like playing a sound, showing a sprite, or broadcasting a message.

Dependencies:
* T16.G3.01: Add a button widget to the stage
* T06.G3.02: Build a key‑press script that controls a sprite


ID: T16.G3.03
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Add a label widget to display text
Description: Use the "add label widget" block to create a text display area on the stage. Set the label's name, initial text content, and position. Labels are used to show information to the user (scores, messages, instructions).

Dependencies:
* T16.G3.01: Add a button widget to the stage


ID: T16.G3.04
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Update label text dynamically
Description: Use the "set widget value" block to change a label's displayed text while the program runs. Connect label updates to events (button clicks, variable changes) to show dynamic information like scores or status messages.

Dependencies:
* T16.G3.03: Add a label widget to display text
* T09.G3.01: Create and use a numeric variable for score or count


ID: T16.G3.05
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Add a textbox widget for user input
Description: Use the "add textbox widget" block to create an input field where users can type text. Set the textbox name, placeholder text, and position. Understand the difference between a label (display only) and textbox (user can type).

Dependencies:
* T16.G3.03: Add a label widget to display text


ID: T16.G3.06
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Get text from a textbox widget
Description: Use the "value of widget" block to retrieve the text that a user typed into a textbox. Store the input in a variable or use it directly in other blocks (e.g., display it in a label, use it in a greeting).

Dependencies:
* T16.G3.05: Add a textbox widget for user input
* T09.G3.02: Use a variable in a conditional (if block)


ID: T16.G3.07
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Show and hide widgets
Description: Use the "set widget visible" block to show or hide widgets. Create simple interactions where clicking a button shows or hides other widgets (e.g., show instructions when "Help" is clicked, hide a menu after selection).

Dependencies:
* T16.G3.02: Handle a button click event
* T08.G3.01: Use a simple if in a script


ID: T16.G3.08
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Position and resize widgets
Description: Use the "move widget to" and "set widget size" blocks to control where widgets appear and how large they are. Arrange multiple widgets to create a simple layout (e.g., title at top, buttons below, input fields in the middle).

Dependencies:
* T16.G3.07: Show and hide widgets


ID: T16.G4.01
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Style widget text properties
Description: Use the "set widget text style" block to change font family, font size, text color, and alignment (left, center, right) of widget text. Create visually appealing labels and buttons with appropriate text formatting.

Dependencies:
* T16.G3.08: Position and resize widgets
* T06.G3.08: Fix a behavior that runs at the wrong time


ID: T16.G4.02
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Style widget appearance
Description: Use the "set widget style" block to customize widget backgrounds (color or image), borders (width, color, style), and corner radius. Create buttons and labels that match a visual theme or stand out for emphasis.

Dependencies:
* T16.G4.01: Style widget text properties


ID: T16.G4.03
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Add a dropdown menu widget
Description: Use the "add dropdown widget" block to create a selection menu with multiple options. Populate the dropdown with a list of choices. Understand when to use dropdowns vs buttons (many options, single selection).

Dependencies:
* T16.G4.02: Style widget appearance
* T10.G3.01: Loop through and process each item in a list


ID: T16.G4.04
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Get the selected value from a dropdown
Description: Use the "value of widget" block to retrieve which option the user selected from a dropdown menu. Use the selected value in conditionals or to update other parts of the interface.

Dependencies:
* T16.G4.03: Add a dropdown menu widget
* T08.G3.04: Trace code with a single if/else


ID: T16.G4.05
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Add a slider widget for numeric input
Description: Use the "add slider widget" block to create a slider that users can drag to select a numeric value within a range. Set the minimum, maximum, and initial values. Sliders are useful for settings like volume, speed, or size.

Dependencies:
* T16.G4.02: Style widget appearance


ID: T16.G4.06
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Read and respond to slider value changes
Description: Use the "when widget value changed" event and "value of widget" block to detect when a user moves a slider and get its current value. Update other elements in real-time as the slider moves (e.g., adjust sprite size, change speed).

Dependencies:
* T16.G4.05: Add a slider widget for numeric input
* T09.G3.04: Trace code with variables to predict outcomes


ID: T16.G4.07
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Add checkbox and radio button widgets
Description: Use the "add checkbox widget" and "add radio button widget" blocks to create toggle options. Checkboxes allow multiple selections; radio buttons in a group allow only one selection. Use these for settings or preferences.

Dependencies:
* T16.G4.04: Get the selected value from a dropdown
* T08.G3.05: Fix a condition that uses the wrong operator


ID: T16.G4.08
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Build a simple settings panel
Description: Combine multiple widget types (labels, checkboxes, sliders, dropdowns) to create a settings or preferences panel. Use widget values to control program behavior (e.g., sound on/off checkbox, difficulty dropdown, volume slider).

Dependencies:
* T16.G4.07: Add checkbox and radio button widgets

ID: T16.G6.01
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Evaluate an interface for usability
Description: Students examine an existing interface (a simple app screenshot) and identify issues or strengths: Are buttons clearly labeled? Is the layout intuitive? Are colors accessible for colorblind users? They learn to think like a UX designer and consider diverse users.

Dependencies:
* T16.G5.03: Build a leaderboard or high‑score display


ID: T16.G6.02
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Design an interface based on user feedback
Description: Students design an initial interface (buttons, labels, layout), ask peers or a teacher to try it, gather feedback on usability, and then modify the design to address the feedback. This introduces the iterative design process.

Dependencies:
* T16.G6.01: Evaluate an interface for usability


ID: T16.G6.03
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Use color and contrast to improve readability
Description: Students apply color theory to interface design: choosing high-contrast text and backgrounds for readability, avoiding color combinations that are difficult for colorblind users, and using color to highlight important elements (e.g., a red button for "Stop").

Dependencies:
* T16.G5.03: Build a leaderboard or high‑score display
* T16.G4.02: Style widget appearance


ID: T16.G6.04
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Create an interface that works on different screen sizes
Description: Students learn that interfaces may be viewed on different devices (tablets, phones, computers) and adjust their layouts to be flexible. They position buttons and labels using percentages or relative sizing rather than fixed positions.

Dependencies:
* T16.G5.01: Create a multi‑screen app with a navigation interface
* T16.G4.01: Style widget text properties

Topic: T16 – User Interfaces

Description: Students create a text input field where users can type a query, and the interface filters or searches a list of items (e.g., a player inventory, a menu of options) to show only matching results. This is a real-world UI pattern.

Dependencies:
* T16.G6.04: Create an interface that works on different screen sizes

Topic: T16 – User Interfaces

Description: Students consider accessibility needs (e.g., text size for low vision, keyboard controls for mobility challenges, colorblind-friendly palettes) and redesign an interface to accommodate multiple ability types. They learn to design inclusively from the start.

Dependencies:
* T16.G6.03: Use color and contrast to improve readability
* T16.G6.04: Create an interface that works on different screen sizes

Description: Students design a help or tutorial interface within a game, including explanatory labels, step-by-step instructions, images/animations, and a "Next" button to guide the player through mechanics or controls.

Skill: Design a wizard or step-by-step interface
Description: Students build a "wizard" interface that guides users through a multi-step process (e.g., character creation, game setup, checkout) with Previous/Next buttons, progress indicators, and validation at each step. They manage state across multiple screens.

Dependencies:

Skill: Implement dynamic content loading in a UI
Description: Students design an interface where selecting an option dynamically loads and displays related content (e.g., clicking a character name displays their stats, clicking a level number shows the level preview). Content is retrieved from lists or variables.

Dependencies:
* T16.G7.02: Implement a search or filter interface
* T16.G7.01: Build a data collection interface (survey or questionnaire)
* T09.G6.01: Use variables to represent real‑world quantities


ID: T16.G8.03
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Analyze UI design patterns and their effectiveness
Description: Students examine two different interface designs for the same task (e.g., two layouts for a settings menu, two ways to input a number) and evaluate which is more effective based on clarity, ease of use, and aesthetics. They write a brief analysis.

Dependencies:
* T16.G7.03: Design an accessible interface for users with different abilities
* T16.G6.02: Design an interface based on user feedback


ID: T16.G8.04
Topic: T16 – User Interfaces
Skill: Document and refine a UI design based on usability testing
Description: Students conduct user testing of their interface (having peers try to complete a task using their interface, noting where they struggle), document observations, and refactor the interface to resolve usability issues. This reinforces the human-centered design cycle.

Dependencies:
* T16.G8.03: Analyze UI design patterns and their effectiveness
* T16.G6.02: Design an interface based on user feedback


ID: T17.G3.01
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Observe position changes from motion blocks
Description: Students observe how motion blocks (move, glide) change a sprite's position over time. They describe motion as "changing position" and predict where a sprite will be after motion blocks run.

Dependencies:
* T06.G3.01: Build a green‑flag script that runs a 3–5 block sequence


ID: T17.G3.02
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Predict direction and distance of sprite motion
Description: Students predict which direction a sprite will move and approximately how far, given a sequence of motion blocks. They develop intuition for motion before variables are introduced.

Dependencies:
* T17.G3.01: Observe position changes from motion blocks


ID: T17.G4.01
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Simulate falling with repeated motion
Description: Students create a simple falling animation by repeatedly moving a sprite down in a loop. They observe that the sprite appears to "fall" due to gravity conceptually, preparing them for velocity-based motion.

Dependencies:
* T07.G3.01: Use a counted repeat loop
* T17.G3.02: Predict direction and distance of sprite motion


ID: T17.G4.02
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Explain speed as position change over time
Description: Students explain that speed means "how much position changes each time the loop runs." They compare fast vs slow motion by changing the step size in a loop.

Dependencies:
* T09.G3.04: Trace code with variables to predict outcomes
* T17.G4.01: Simulate falling with repeated motion


ID: T17.G5.01
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Choose manual vs engine-based physics
Description: Students compare CreatiCode project briefs (platformer, UI animation, top-down maze, pinball machine) and choose whether to stick with manual velocity variables or enable the 2D physics extension. They explain the decision for each brief based on project requirements.

Dependencies:
* T05.G4.05: Plan a simulation with defined inputs and outputs
* T17.G4.02: Explain speed as position change over time


ID: T17.G5.02
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Track gravity with velocity variables
Description: Students build a loop that stores a sprite's y-velocity in a variable, subtracts a gravity constant each frame, then adds the velocity to the sprite's y-position. This manual approach mirrors classic Scratch tutorials and prepares students for physics debugging.

Dependencies:
* T07.G3.05: Fix a loop that runs too many or too few times
* T09.G3.04: Trace code with variables to predict outcomes
* T17.G5.01: Choose manual vs engine-based physics


ID: T17.G5.03
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Use horizontal speed and friction variables
Description: Students add an x-velocity variable, respond to arrow keys to change it, and multiply by a friction factor (e.g., 0.9) each tick so motion glides to a stop. This prepares students for platformer mechanics.

Dependencies:
* T09.G4.03: Use multiple variables in a single script
* T17.G5.02: Track gravity with velocity variables


ID: T17.G5.04
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Code a manual bounce with energy loss
Description: Students write a conditional that checks for ground contact, multiplies the y-velocity by a negative damping factor (e.g., -0.6), and sends the sprite back up with reduced height. This cements physics vocabulary before using the engine's restitution.

Dependencies:
* T08.G3.01: Use a simple if in a script
* T17.G5.02: Track gravity with velocity variables


ID: T17.G5.05
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Initialize a 2D physics world
Description: Students add the `initialize 2D physics world with gravity x [0] y [-100]` block, set appropriate gravity values, and confirm the debug overlay shows the world running. They understand that no physics behavior occurs until this block executes.

Dependencies:
* T06.G3.01: Build a green‑flag script that runs a 3–5 block sequence
* T17.G5.01: Choose manual vs engine-based physics


ID: T17.G5.06
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Attach a dynamic body to a sprite
Description: Students convert a sprite to a dynamic physics body using `behave as a [dynamic] [object] shape [Box] debug [Yes]`. They observe the sprite fall and stop when it hits the stage floor, confirming the physics world affects it.

Dependencies:
* T17.G5.05: Initialize a 2D physics world


ID: T17.G5.06.01
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Select appropriate body shapes (Box, Ball, ConvexHull)
Description: Students choose the appropriate collision shape for different sprites: Box for rectangular objects, Ball for circular objects, and ConvexHull for irregular shapes. They understand that shape affects collision accuracy and performance.

Dependencies:
* T17.G5.06: Attach a dynamic body to a sprite


ID: T17.G5.06.02
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Create sensor bodies for trigger zones
Description: Students create sensor bodies using `behave as a [dynamic] [sensor]` that detect overlaps without causing physical collisions. They use sensors for trigger zones, collectible detection areas, and checkpoint markers.

Dependencies:
* T17.G5.06.01: Select appropriate body shapes (Box, Ball, ConvexHull)


ID: T17.G5.07
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Build fixed boundaries for floors and walls
Description: Students add fixed physics bodies to floor or wall sprites using `behave as a [fixed] [object]` so falling or sliding objects stop on contact. They learn to use fixed bodies for geometry that should not move.

Dependencies:
* T17.G5.05: Initialize a 2D physics world


ID: T17.G5.08
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Apply an impulse to jump or push
Description: Students use `apply impulse [force] in direction [90]` to make a dynamic sprite jump in response to input. They control impulse strength so the sprite clears a target platform height.

Dependencies:
* T06.G4.01: Use multiple event handlers in the same sprite
* T17.G5.06: Attach a dynamic body to a sprite


ID: T17.G5.08.01
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Distinguish forces from impulses
Description: Students compare `add force in direction` (applied continuously each frame) with `apply impulse in direction` (applied once instantly). They use forces for sustained thrust (jetpack) and impulses for sudden actions (jump, kick).

Dependencies:
* T17.G5.08: Apply an impulse to jump or push


ID: T17.G5.09
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Configure density for mass control
Description: Students adjust density using `update density [value] friction % restitution %` to control how heavy a sprite feels. They understand that density × area = mass and experiment with light vs heavy objects in collisions.

Dependencies:
* T17.G5.06: Attach a dynamic body to a sprite


ID: T17.G5.10
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Trace simple 2D physics motion
Description: Students read a small table showing gravity, density, starting height, and time elapsed, then choose the correct statement about where the sprite will be (e.g., "lands on the platform," "still in the air," "passed through the floor").

Dependencies:
* T09.G3.04: Trace code with variables to predict outcomes
* T17.G5.06: Attach a dynamic body to a sprite


ID: T17.G5.11
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Debug missing physics setup
Description: Students open a buggy project where the player never falls because the physics world was not initialized or the body was left as fixed. They inspect the scripts, identify the missing setup, and re-test.

Dependencies:
* T17.G5.06: Attach a dynamic body to a sprite
* T17.G5.07: Build fixed boundaries for floors and walls


ID: T17.G6.01
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Configure surface friction parameters
Description: Students adjust the friction percentage using `update density friction [value]% restitution %` and measure how far objects slide on different surfaces. They learn to map friction values to sliding distances through systematic testing.

Dependencies:
* T08.G3.01: Use a simple if in a script
* T09.G3.04: Trace code with variables to predict outcomes
* T17.G5.10: Trace simple 2D physics motion


ID: T17.G6.02
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Control restitution (bounce) parameters
Description: Students modify the restitution percentage and measure bounce heights. They learn the relationship between restitution values (0-100%) and energy conservation in collisions: 0% = no bounce, 100% = full bounce.

Dependencies:
* T09.G3.04: Trace code with variables to predict outcomes
* T17.G6.01: Configure surface friction parameters


ID: T17.G6.03
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Build a kinematic moving platform
Description: Students create a platform that moves on a fixed path while still colliding with players. They use `set x speed` and `set y speed` to control platform motion directly rather than relying on physics forces.

Dependencies:
* T07.G3.05: Fix a loop that runs too many or too few times
* T17.G5.10: Trace simple 2D physics motion


ID: T17.G6.04
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Detect collisions for scoring or triggers
Description: Students use `broadcast [message] when colliding with [sprite]` to listen for collision events between sprites. They run scoring or state-change scripts in response to collisions (player hits coin, ball hits bumper).

Dependencies:
* T06.G4.01: Use multiple event handlers in the same sprite
* T17.G5.10: Trace simple 2D physics motion


ID: T17.G6.04.01
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Use ground detection for platformer jumping
Description: Students enable `turn on ground detection within distance [value] debug [Yes]` and use the `<in collision below>` reporter to allow jumping only when grounded. They configure detection distance and debug detection issues.

Dependencies:
* T17.G6.04: Detect collisions for scoring or triggers


ID: T17.G6.05
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Use collision groups to filter interactions
Description: Students use `add to collision group [0-15]` and `disable collision with group [G]` so the player can pass through certain objects (collectibles) while still hitting others (hazards). They reason about selective interactions.

Dependencies:
* T08.G4.01: Write a condition that uses and/or
* T17.G6.04: Detect collisions for scoring or triggers


ID: T17.G6.05.01
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Use dominance groups for one-way interactions
Description: Students use `set dominance group to [value]` (-127 to 127) to create one-way pushers where high-dominance objects push low-dominance objects without being pushed back themselves.

Dependencies:
* T17.G6.05: Use collision groups to filter interactions


ID: T17.G6.06
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Blend manual and engine sprites in a level
Description: Students keep manual scripts (e.g., scrolling backgrounds, UI elements) running alongside physics bodies in the same project without conflicts. They ensure manual sprites are not converted to physics bodies.

Dependencies:
* T17.G5.10: Trace simple 2D physics motion
* T17.G5.11: Debug missing physics setup


ID: T17.G6.07
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Debug unstable physics behavior
Description: Students diagnose why a sprite jitters, sinks through a platform, or flies off-screen (e.g., density too low, conflicting impulses, missing collision groups) and adjust parameters to stabilize the scene.

Dependencies:
* T17.G6.01: Configure surface friction parameters
* T17.G6.02: Control restitution (bounce) parameters


ID: T17.G6.08
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Compare simulations to real-world motion
Description: Students record bounce heights or slide distances in CreatiCode, compare them to expected real-world results, and discuss how closely the simulation matches reality and what simplifications the physics engine makes.

Dependencies:
* T08.G3.01: Use a simple if in a script
* T09.G3.04: Trace code with variables to predict outcomes
* T17.G5.10: Trace simple 2D physics motion


ID: T17.G7.01
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Launch a configurable projectile
Description: Students create a launcher where users set angle and power using sliders. The projectile receives an initial impulse using `apply impulse [force] in direction [angle]` that produces a parabolic arc toward targets.

Dependencies:
* T08.G5.01: Fix a condition that uses the wrong operator
* T09.G5.01: Create and use a numeric variable for score or count
* T17.G6.08: Compare simulations to real-world motion


ID: T17.G7.02
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Combine multiple forces simultaneously
Description: Students use `add force in direction` to apply two or more forces in the same frame (gravity + constant wind, gravity + player thrust). They predict and observe the resulting curved motion paths.

Dependencies:
* T17.G5.08.01: Distinguish forces from impulses
* T17.G6.07: Debug unstable physics behavior
* T17.G6.08: Compare simulations to real-world motion


ID: T17.G7.03
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Simulate drag or resistance
Description: Students implement drag effects using either manual force calculations (applying force opposite to velocity) or the built-in `set damping factor for movement [value]%` block. They compare damping values for different media (air, water, honey).

Dependencies:
* T17.G6.07: Debug unstable physics behavior
* T17.G6.08: Compare simulations to real-world motion


ID: T17.G7.03.01
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Use built-in damping for drag effects
Description: Students use `set damping factor for movement [M]% rotation [R]%` to simulate air resistance or water friction without manual force calculations. They tune damping percentages for desired slowdown behavior.

Dependencies:
* T17.G7.03: Simulate drag or resistance


ID: T17.G7.04
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Build chains or stacks of physics objects
Description: Students create stacks of boxes or chains of linked sprites and explore how forces propagate through the system when one element is pushed. They observe how density affects collision outcomes.

Dependencies:
* T17.G6.07: Debug unstable physics behavior
* T17.G6.08: Compare simulations to real-world motion


ID: T17.G7.04.01
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Use rotation speed and torque
Description: Students use `set rotation speed [value]` for direct rotation control and `apply torque impulse [value]` for physics-driven rotation. They build spinning objects, rotating platforms, and objects that tumble realistically.

Dependencies:
* T17.G7.04: Build chains or stacks of physics objects


ID: T17.G7.05
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Instrument and graph motion data
Description: Students record motion data from a sprite every few frames using `(x speed)` and `(y speed)` reporters, store values in lists, and create a graph. They use the graph to confirm constant acceleration or spot errors.

Dependencies:
* T10.G5.01: Add and remove items from a list
* T17.G6.07: Debug unstable physics behavior
* T17.G6.08: Compare simulations to real-world motion


ID: T17.G7.05.01
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Read velocity and mass reporters
Description: Students use the reporter blocks `(x speed)`, `(y speed)`, `(mass)`, and `(ground slope)` to display real-time physics data on screen. They use this data for UI displays, conditional logic, and debugging.

Dependencies:
* T17.G7.05: Instrument and graph motion data


ID: T17.G7.06
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Model a real-world physics scenario
Description: Students choose a real phenomenon (bouncing ball, swinging pendulum, sliding object) and build a CreatiCode simulation that approximates it. They explain which physics properties (gravity, friction, restitution) they tuned to mimic reality.

Dependencies:
* T08.G5.01: Fix a condition that uses the wrong operator
* T09.G5.01: Create and use a numeric variable for score or count
* T17.G6.08: Compare simulations to real-world motion


ID: T17.G7.07
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Evaluate whether a simulation meets requirements
Description: Students are given target requirements (e.g., "ball must clear the second bumper but stop before the third") and test a simulation against them. They examine logged data and decide if requirements were met, citing evidence.

Dependencies:
* T17.G6.07: Debug unstable physics behavior
* T17.G6.08: Compare simulations to real-world motion


ID: T17.G8.01
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Design and balance a physics-based arcade game
Description: Students design a launcher + target game (Angry Birds–style) with multiple levels of difficulty. They test and adjust physics parameters (gravity, impulse strength, object density) to make gameplay fair but challenging.

Dependencies:
* T07.G6.01: Trace nested loops with variables
* T08.G6.01: Use conditionals to control simulation steps
* T17.G7.06: Model a real-world physics scenario


ID: T17.G8.02
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Implement fixed joints for connected objects
Description: Students use `fix relative position to [sprite]` to weld sprites together so they move as a single rigid unit. Examples: compound objects, multi-part characters, towed vehicles.

Dependencies:
* T09.G6.01: Use variables to represent real‑world quantities
* T17.G7.06: Model a real-world physics scenario


ID: T17.G8.02.01
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Implement revolute joints for hinges
Description: Students use `set [sprite] as rotation axis with offset x [X] y [Y]` to create hinged objects like doors, seesaws, and pendulums. They configure rotation behavior with `set rotation axis speed [S] damping factor [D]%`.

Dependencies:
* T17.G8.02: Implement fixed joints for connected objects


ID: T17.G8.02.02
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Implement prismatic joints for sliding
Description: Students use `allow [Horizontal/Vertical] sliding relative to [sprite] range from [min] to [max]` to create pistons, sliding doors, and spring-loaded platforms with configurable movement limits.

Dependencies:
* T17.G8.02.01: Implement revolute joints for hinges


ID: T17.G8.03
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Build automated physics regression tests
Description: Students create scripts that spawn test objects, run the simulation for a set time, and assert that positions, velocities, or collision counts stay within tolerances. This guards against regressions when modifying physics code.

Dependencies:
* T08.G6.01: Use conditionals to control simulation steps
* T17.G7.07: Evaluate whether a simulation meets requirements


ID: T17.G8.04
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Optimize a physics scene for performance
Description: Students profile a busy physics scene and implement optimizations: using simpler collision shapes (Box instead of ConvexHull), reducing active object count, disabling unnecessary collision groups, and hiding debug overlays.

Dependencies:
* T07.G6.01: Trace nested loops with variables
* T17.G7.06: Model a real-world physics scenario
* T17.G7.07: Evaluate whether a simulation meets requirements


ID: T17.G8.04.01
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Enable CCD for fast-moving objects
Description: Students use `enable collision detection as a fast object [Yes]` (Continuous Collision Detection) for bullets, fast balls, or other high-speed objects that might tunnel through thin walls at normal update rates.

Dependencies:
* T17.G8.04: Optimize a physics scene for performance


ID: T17.G8.05
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Control gravity scale and time speed
Description: Students use `set gravity scale [value]%` to create floaty zones or reverse gravity areas, and `set physics time speed [value]%` to create slow-motion or fast-forward effects for dramatic game moments.

Dependencies:
* T17.G7.06: Model a real-world physics scenario


ID: T17.G8.06
Topic: T17 – 2D Motion & Physics
Skill: Use instrumentation data to tune difficulty
Description: Students log player attempts (launch angle, power, success/fail), analyze the dataset, and retune physics parameters (gravity, impulse strength, target size) to achieve a desired win rate. They connect physics tweaks to game analytics.

Dependencies:
* T09.G6.01: Use variables to represent real‑world quantities
* T17.G7.06: Model a real-world physics scenario


ID: T18.G3.01

Description: Students read a labeled axis diagram or CreatiCode gizmo and identify which axis controls width, height, and depth, linking math vocabulary to the 3D stage.

ID: T18.G3.02

Description: Students compare front/top/side snapshots of the same object arrangement and match each snapshot to the correct camera icon, understanding how viewpoint affects what they see before coding cameras.

Dependencies:
* T18.G3.01: Interpret 3D axis directions


ID: T18.G3.03
Topic: T18 – 3D Worlds & Games
Skill: Initialize a 3D scene with default lighting
Description: Students add a `when green flag clicked` script that calls the CreatiCode `initialize 3D scene [SCENETYPE]` block (choosing a scene type like Empty, Grass Land, or City) so every run begins with a clean scene including default camera and lighting.

Dependencies:
* T18.G3.02: Match camera views to 3D layouts
* T07.G3.02: Trace a script with a simple loop
* T03.G3.03: Create a 3‑panel storyboard for a project


ID: T18.G3.04
Topic: T18 – 3D Worlds & Games
Skill: Add primitive shapes with 3D blocks
Description: Students use the `add box`, `add sphere`, and `add cylinder` blocks to place primitives in the scene and adjust their size parameters in x/y/z dimensions.

Dependencies:
* T18.G3.03: Initialize a 3D scene with default lighting


ID: T18.G3.05
Topic: T18 – 3D Worlds & Games
Skill: Position shapes using x/y/z coordinates
Description: Students set `x`, `y`, and `z` values (or use `go to x:y:z`) to move an object to a target location, connecting coordinate plans from earlier math/diagram skills (T02/T25) to actual blocks.

Dependencies:
* T18.G3.04: Add primitive shapes with 3D blocks
* T09.G3.02: Use a variable in a conditional (if block)


ID: T18.G3.06
Topic: T18 – 3D Worlds & Games
Skill: Change shape colors or textures
Description: Students use 3D styling blocks (set color, set texture, adjust opacity) to differentiate objects such as making the ground green and a sphere metallic.

Dependencies:
* T18.G3.05: Position shapes using x/y/z coordinates
* T07.G3.03: Build a forever loop for simple animation
* T03.G3.04: Match storyboard panels to project scenes


ID: T18.G3.07
Topic: T18 – 3D Worlds & Games
Skill: Move a 3D player with keyboard input
Description: Students build a `forever` loop that checks arrow keys (or WASD) and `change x/z` so a player cube can walk around the scene.

Dependencies:
* T18.G3.06: Change shape colors or textures
* T09.G3.03: Debug missing or wrong variable updates


ID: T18.G3.08
Topic: T18 – 3D Worlds & Games
Skill: Trace a short 3D script to predict positions
Description: Students read a short 3D script that changes `x`, `y`, and rotation values and predict the final position/orientation without running it, reinforcing spatial reasoning.

Dependencies:
* T18.G3.07: Move a 3D player with keyboard input
* T11.G3.01: Understand when to use custom blocks vs loops
* T07.G3.04: Use repeat‑until to reach a simple goal

Topic: T18 – 3D Worlds & Games

Description: Students create looping animations for props (windmill spinning, lights pulsing, platforms bobbing) by combining `forever` loops with the `set speed` block for rotation or position changes.

ID: T18.G5.01
Topic: T18 – 3D Worlds & Games
Skill: Initialize a 3D physics world
Description: Students add the CreatiCode 3D physics initialization block `enable physics for scene with gravity`, set gravity for the Z-axis (typically -10), and verify objects respond to physics by optionally enabling debug visualization on physics bodies.

Dependencies:
* T18.G4.01: Compose a multi-part 3D scene with primitives

ID: T18.G5.02
Topic: T18 – 3D Worlds & Games
Skill: Attach static and dynamic physics bodies
Description: Students configure which shapes are static (floors, walls) and which are dynamic (player, crates) by using the `add [shape] physics body` block with mass, restitution, and friction settings so objects react to gravity.

Dependencies:
* T18.G5.01: Initialize a 3D physics world
* T07.G3.05: Fix a loop that runs too many or too few times
* T14.G3.01: Move a sprite with arrow keys (4 directions)


ID: T18.G5.03
Topic: T18 – 3D Worlds & Games
Skill: Detect physics collisions to collect items
Description: Students use collision detection blocks (e.g., `names of physics bodies in contact` or `broadcast on collision`) to change score, remove coins, or play sounds when the player touches collectibles.

Dependencies:
* T18.G5.02: Attach static and dynamic physics bodies
* T18.G4.05: Animate scenery elements with loops


ID: T18.G5.04
Topic: T18 – 3D Worlds & Games
Skill: Use nested loops to arrange 3D objects in grids
Description: Students apply nested loops to stamp or spawn platforms, trees, or tiles at evenly spaced coordinates, optionally varying height for stepped terrain.

Dependencies:
* T18.G4.01: Compose a multi-part 3D scene with primitives
* T18.G4.05: Animate scenery elements with loops

Description: Students use material blocks (`update texture`, `update color`) to apply tileable textures, adjust unit size for UV scaling, or mix colors and emission properties so surfaces like walls or roads look realistic.

ID: T19.G5.02
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Add a sprite to the multiplayer game world
Description: Students use the `add this sprite to game as a [Dynamic/Static] [Rectangle/Circle]` block to register a sprite with the game server. They understand that Dynamic sprites can move while Static sprites remain fixed, and that the shape determines collision detection.

Dependencies:
* T19.G5.01: Host or join a CreatiCode multiplayer lobby


ID: T19.G5.03
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Initialize a sprite when it joins the game using "when added to game"
Description: Students use the `when added to game` hat block to run initialization code when a sprite is confirmed registered by the server. They set starting positions, display names, or announce arrivals to other players.

Dependencies:
* T19.G5.02: Add a sprite to the multiplayer game world


ID: T19.G5.04
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Broadcast messages to all players in a multiplayer session
Description: Students use the `broadcast [MESSAGE] with parameter [PARAMETER] mode [MODE]` block to send messages to all players. They choose between "All Sprites" mode (all sprites including replicates) or "Exclude Replicate" mode (only original sprites) based on the use case.

Dependencies:
* T19.G5.03: Initialize a sprite when it joins the game using "when added to game"


ID: T19.G5.05
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Check connection status and display feedback to the player
Description: Students use the `connected to game` boolean block to check whether they are properly connected. They display appropriate messages (e.g., "Connected!" or "Reconnecting...") and disable game controls when disconnected.

Dependencies:
* T19.G5.01: Host or join a CreatiCode multiplayer lobby
* T08.G3.01: Use a simple if in a script


ID: T19.G6.01
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Synchronize player movement using synchronized speed blocks
Description: Students use the `synchronously set speed x (X) y (Y)` or `synchronously set speed (SPEED) dir (DIR)` blocks to move sprites so that all players see the same motion. They understand that the server coordinates movement across all connected clients.

Dependencies:
* T19.G5.03: Initialize a sprite when it joins the game using "when added to game"
* T19.G5.05: Check connection status and display feedback to the player
* T31.G5.01: Trace how a device reaches an online service


ID: T19.G6.02
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Handle multiplayer collisions using synchronized touch events
Description: Students use the `when touching [SPRITENAME] will [stop/pass] and trigger [MESSAGE] with parameter [PARAMETER]` block to detect collisions between multiplayer sprites. They configure whether sprites should stop or pass through on contact and handle the triggered message.

Dependencies:
* T19.G6.01: Synchronize player movement using synchronized speed blocks


ID: T19.G6.03
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Create shared world objects that stay synchronized during a session
Description: Students add static sprites (coins, doors, obstacles) to the game world and track their state. When a player interacts with an object, they broadcast the change so all clients show the same world state.

Dependencies:
* T19.G5.02: Add a sprite to the multiplayer game world
* T19.G5.04: Broadcast messages to all players in a multiplayer session
* T09.G3.01: Create and use a numeric variable for score or count


ID: T19.G6.04
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Display a synchronized scoreboard for multiplayer sessions
Description: Students maintain score variables that update across all clients when any player earns points. They use broadcasts or synchronized variables to ensure all players see the same scoreboard.

Dependencies:
* T19.G5.04: Broadcast messages to all players in a multiplayer session
* T09.G3.01: Create and use a numeric variable for score or count


ID: T19.G6.05
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Handle player join and leave events for dynamic game lobbies
Description: Students use the `list players in game` block to detect when new players join or existing players leave. They spawn or remove sprites accordingly and send welcome messages or update the player list display.

Dependencies:
* T19.G5.03: Initialize a sprite when it joins the game using "when added to game"
* T19.G5.04: Broadcast messages to all players in a multiplayer session
* T10.G3.03: Add and remove items from a list


ID: T19.G7.01
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Build a cooperative puzzle with shared progress counters
Description: Students design a multiplayer task where players must work together toward shared goals (e.g., both press switches simultaneously). They maintain progress counters that all players can see and update.

Dependencies:
* T19.G6.03: Create shared world objects that stay synchronized during a session
* T19.G6.04: Display a synchronized scoreboard for multiplayer sessions


ID: T19.G7.02
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Implement a ready-up system before the game starts
Description: Students create a lobby where players click a "Ready" button that broadcasts their status. The host monitors the player list and starts the game only when all connected players have marked themselves ready.

Dependencies:
* T19.G6.05: Handle player join and leave events for dynamic game lobbies
* T19.G5.04: Broadcast messages to all players in a multiplayer session


ID: T19.G7.03
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Choose what data to synchronize versus keep local
Description: Students decide which variables should sync across all clients (scores, positions) versus stay local (UI state, sounds). They use broadcasts for event-driven sync and synchronized blocks for continuous updates.

Dependencies:
* T19.G6.01: Synchronize player movement using synchronized speed blocks
* T19.G5.04: Broadcast messages to all players in a multiplayer session


ID: T19.G7.04
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Scale game logic to handle variable player counts
Description: Students refactor scripts to loop over the player list when creating sprites, updating displays, or distributing game objectives. The game works correctly whether 2, 4, or more players are connected.

Dependencies:
* T19.G6.05: Handle player join and leave events for dynamic game lobbies
* T07.G5.01: Use a loop to repeat a task an exact number of times


ID: T19.G7.05
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Balance starting conditions and scoring for fairness
Description: Students audit spawn points, turn order, and scoring rules to identify and eliminate built-in advantages. They test with multiple players and document how changes improve game balance.

Dependencies:
* T19.G7.01: Build a cooperative puzzle with shared progress counters
* T19.G6.04: Display a synchronized scoreboard for multiplayer sessions


ID: T19.G8.01
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Implement team assignment or simple matchmaking
Description: Students automatically assign players to teams based on join order, player count, or role selection. They ensure teams are balanced in size and update assignments when players join or leave.

Dependencies:
* T19.G7.04: Scale game logic to handle variable player counts
* T19.G6.05: Handle player join and leave events for dynamic game lobbies
* T07.G6.01: Trace nested loops with variables


ID: T19.G8.02
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Implement host-authoritative validation to prevent cheating
Description: Students restructure their game so clients request score changes or moves, but only the host validates and applies them. The host rejects impossible actions (teleporting, instant kills) to maintain fair play.

Dependencies:
* T19.G7.03: Choose what data to synchronize versus keep local
* T19.G7.04: Scale game logic to handle variable player counts
* T08.G6.01: Use conditionals to control simulation steps


ID: T19.G8.03
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Persist match data to CreatiCode cloud storage
Description: Students use cloud variables or cloud lists to store final scores, achievements, or unlocks that persist across sessions. They load saved data when players return to show long-term progress.

Dependencies:
* T19.G6.04: Display a synchronized scoreboard for multiplayer sessions
* T09.G6.01: Use variables to represent real‑world quantities
* T31.G6.01: Trace the steps of an HTTP/HTTPS request


ID: T19.G8.04
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Debug message ordering and resolve synchronization issues
Description: Students identify when game state diverges between clients due to message timing. They implement sequence numbers or acknowledgements to ensure all clients process events in the correct order.

Dependencies:
* T19.G7.03: Choose what data to synchronize versus keep local
* T06.G6.01: Trace event execution paths in a multi‑event program
* T13.G6.01: Add print statements to trace variable changes


ID: T19.G8.05
Topic: T19 – Multiplayer Apps: Grade 5–8 Skill List
Skill: Explain the architecture of a multiplayer game system
Description: Students create a diagram showing how their multiplayer game works: player input, host/server processing, message broadcast, and screen updates. They identify potential bottlenecks (too many messages, slow hosts) and propose solutions.

Dependencies:
* T19.G8.02: Implement host-authoritative validation to prevent cheating
* T02.G6.01: Design a flowchart for a simple guessing game
* T06.G6.01: Trace event execution paths in a multi‑event program


ID: T20.GK.01
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Picture pattern detective
Description: Students view short rows of colors/shapes (e.g., sun-moon-sun-moon) and identify which rows follow a clean repeat. They explain what makes a row “repeat” using everyday words.

Dependencies:
* T04.GK.01: Spot a simple repeating pattern




ID: T20.GK.02
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Order art steps with cards
Description: Learners drag picture cards showing steps like “dip brush,” “draw circle,” “sprinkle dots” to match a finished drawing. They reason about sequence without any text.

Dependencies:
* T01.GK.01: Put pictures in order for getting ready for bed




ID: T20.GK.03
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Continue the pattern trail
Description: Students continue a pattern along a dotted path (e.g., flower-heart-flower-heart). They focus on spatial placement and rhythm.

Dependencies:
* T04.GK.01: Spot a simple repeating pattern




ID: T20.GK.04
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Fix the mixed-up art plan
Description: Students look at a 3-step art plan with one incorrect picture (e.g., a color that breaks the pattern) and replace it with the correct one from a small set.

Dependencies:
* T04.GK.01: Spot a simple repeating pattern




ID: T20.G1.01
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Describe the art rule in words
Description: Students view a short repeating design (e.g., two small stars then one big sun) and describe it in everyday language (“two tiny, one big”).

Dependencies:
* T01.GK.01: Put pictures in order for getting ready for bed


ID: T20.G1.02
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Match directions to drawings
Description: Learners match a simple written/audio direction set (“draw a blue square, then add three yellow dots under it”) to the drawing it would produce.

Dependencies:
* T03.GK.02: Match parts to whole objects


ID: T20.G1.03
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Extend a quilt on a grid
Description: Students complete a 2×3 or 3×3 art grid by adding the next tiles so the pattern continues horizontally and vertically.

Dependencies:
* T01.GK.01: Put pictures in order for getting ready for bed


ID: T20.G1.04
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Fix a wrong instruction
Description: Students hear or read a short art direction set with one incorrect step. They must choose the replacement that will restore the target pattern.

Dependencies:
* T01.GK.01: Put pictures in order for getting ready for bed


ID: T20.G2.01
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Use repeat cards in an art recipe
Description: Students compare two instruction sets for the same border: one long (“red square, red square, red square…”) and one that uses a repeat card (“repeat red square 4 times”). They choose the concise, accurate version.

Dependencies:
* T01.G1.04: Predict the next step in a story sequence


ID: T20.G2.02
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Plan mirrored mosaics
Description: Learners arrange tiles on one side of a line and then plan what tiles should appear on the other side so the design is symmetrical.

Dependencies:
* T05.G1.01: Identify what a character needs in a story
* T01.G1.04: Predict the next step in a story sequence


ID: T20.G2.03
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Build layered pattern recipes
Description: Students interpret a two-layer instruction (e.g., "repeat row A three times, then repeat row B once") to build a stacked design out of strips.

Dependencies:
* T20.G2.01: Use repeat cards in an art recipe
* T01.G2.02: Use "repeat" to make directions shorter


ID: T20.G2.04
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Explain how a change affects the art
Description: Students consider "what-if" prompts (e.g., "What happens if the second color changes from blue to green?") and explain how the final pattern would change.

Dependencies:
* T01.G1.04: Predict the next step in a story sequence
* T20.G2.03: Build layered pattern recipes


ID: T20.G3.01
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Translate art recipe cards into blocks
Description: Given a familiar art recipe (e.g., “draw a triangle, change color, repeat”), students select the block stack that matches the steps. This cements the link between unplugged thinking and coding.

Dependencies:
* T07.G3.01: Use a counted repeat loop
* T20.G2.01: Use repeat cards in an art recipe


ID: T20.G3.02
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Program a repeating border with loops
Description: Students write a simple pen program that repeats a sequence (stamp star, move right) using a `repeat` block. They see how loops reduce effort.

Dependencies:
* T20.G3.01: Translate art recipe cards into blocks
* T08.G3.01: Use a simple if in a script
* T18.G3.02: Match camera views to 3D layouts


ID: T20.G3.03
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Tile a grid with nested loops
Description: Learners combine two loops—one for columns, one for rows—to fill a small grid with a pattern tile. This is the first double-loop exposure in an art context.

Dependencies:
* T20.G3.02: Program a repeating border with loops
* T18.G3.03: Initialize a 3D scene with default lighting


ID: T20.G3.04
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Trace a pen loop and predict output
Description: Students read a short script (loop drawing squares) and predict how many shapes or what final layout appears.

Dependencies:
* T20.G3.03: Tile a grid with nested loops
* T08.G3.02: Decide when a single if is enough
* T18.G3.04: Add primitive shapes with 3D blocks


ID: T20.G3.05
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Add simple randomness for variety
Description: Students extend a loop-based drawing by adding `pick random` for pen color or small position shifts, producing playful variations each run.

Dependencies:
* T20.G3.04: Trace a pen loop and predict output
* T09.G3.02: Use a variable in a conditional (if block)
* T07.G3.03: Build a forever loop for simple animation


ID: T20.G4.01
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: **[Technical Skill]** Implement incremental loops for spirals
Description: Students write a loop that increases a variable (distance or angle) each iteration to create mathematical spiral patterns. They focus on the technical implementation of incremental variables and loop mechanics.

Dependencies:
* T07.G3.01: Use a counted repeat loop
* T07.G3.05: Fix a loop that runs too many or too few times
* T09.G3.01: Create and use a numeric variable for score or count
* T20.G3.05: Add simple randomness for variety


ID: T20.G4.02
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: **[Technical Skill]** Implement tessellation with custom blocks
Description: Students create a custom block (introduced in T11.G4.01) that draws a geometric tile pattern, then use nested loops to repeat it across the stage. They focus on modular code structure and coordinate calculations.

Dependencies:
* T07.G3.01: Use a counted repeat loop
* T07.G3.05: Fix a loop that runs too many or too few times
* T20.G3.05: Add simple randomness for variety

ID: T20.G8.05
Topic: T20 – Algorithmic Art & Creative Coding
Skill: Combine multiple algorithms in an art pipeline
Description: Students integrate data, noise/randomness, and animation phases to create a cohesive experience (e.g., start with a data-informed layout, overlay noise-based textures, animate highlights).

Dependencies:
* T06.G6.01: Trace event execution paths in a multi‑event program
* T07.G6.01: Trace nested loops with variables
* T09.G6.01: Use variables to represent real‑world quantities
* T20.G7.05: Implement iterative art rules (L-system lite)


ID: T21.G3.01
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Tell whether media was AI-generated or recorded
Description: Students compare pairs of images or short sounds (one AI-generated, one recorded) and pick which seems AI-made, explaining clues (odd shadows, repeated textures, robotic voice tone).

Dependencies:
* T20.G3.01: Translate art recipe cards into blocks


ID: T21.G4.01
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Choose safe and specific prompts for images
Description: Given a vague or risky image request ("make a person" or "draw my house address"), students rewrite it to be specific, safe, and privacy-friendly (e.g., "Draw a friendly robot in a park, daytime").

Dependencies:
* T08.G3.01: Use a simple if in a script
* T09.G3.04: Trace code with variables to predict outcomes
* T10.G3.03: Add and remove items from a list

ID: T21.G5.01
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Plan which assets should be AI-made vs hand-made
Description: Students see a simple app pitch (storybook, quiz) and choose which assets to request from AI (e.g., varied backdrops) and which to make by hand (e.g., main character for consistent look), noting one reason for each choice.

Dependencies:
* T09.G3.04: Trace code with variables to predict outcomes
* T10.G3.03: Add and remove items from a list
* T21.G4.01: Choose safe and specific prompts for images


ID: T21.G5.02
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Generate a single AI image using a simple prompt
Description: Students use the `OpenAI DALL-E: generate costume image` block to create one image from a descriptive prompt. They observe how the AI interprets their words and compare the result to their expectation.

Dependencies:
* T06.G3.01: Build a green‑flag script that runs a 3–5 block sequence
* T21.G4.01: Choose safe and specific prompts for images


ID: T21.G5.03
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Use AI text-to-speech to read text aloud
Description: Students use the `say [TEXT] in [LANGUAGE]` block to have the computer speak a sentence aloud. They experiment with different languages and voice types to hear how text-to-speech works.

Dependencies:
* T06.G3.01: Build a green‑flag script that runs a 3–5 block sequence
* T21.G3.01: Tell whether media was AI-generated or recorded


ID: T21.G6.01
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Plan a mixed-source asset kit for a project
Description: Students list all assets needed for a planned project (costumes, backdrops, sounds), categorize each as "AI-generated," "hand-created," or "library," and provide one reason for each choice (e.g., "AI for varied backgrounds, hand-drawn for the main character's consistent look").

Dependencies:

Description: Students turn vague prompt starters (e.g., "dragon in a cave") into structured prompts that include subject, action, camera angle, palette, and mood so the resulting art matches UI expectations. They reuse the same structure for multiple assets to keep scenes consistent.

ID: T21.G6.03
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Build a prompt test bench inside CreatiCode
Description: Students design a screen with a text input, dropdown style selector, and gallery of preview sprites. Pressing a "Generate" button triggers the `OpenAI DALL-E: generate costume image` block, loads three variations, and logs each prompt + URL in a table so the designer can choose a winner.

Dependencies:
* T06.G3.01: Build a green‑flag script that runs a 3–5 block sequence

ID: T21.G6.04
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Iterate when an AI output fails requirements
Description: Students practice reading a failed generation (wrong colors, missing character, awkward proportions), identifying the cause (prompt missing detail, wrong style, conflicting terms), and rewriting the prompt to address the issue. They compare "before/after" versions to show how iteration improves fit.

Dependencies:
* T07.G3.01: Use a counted repeat loop
* T08.G3.01: Use a simple if in a script
* T09.G3.04: Trace code with variables to predict outcomes

ID: T21.G6.05
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Use AI speech recognition to capture user voice input
Description: Students use `start recognizing speech`, `end speech recognition`, and `text from speech` blocks to record their voice and convert it to text. They verify the transcription accuracy and understand speech-to-text limitations.

Dependencies:
* T06.G4.01: Use broadcast to coordinate sprite actions
* T21.G5.03: Use AI text-to-speech to read text aloud


ID: T21.G6.06
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Check user input with AI content moderation
Description: Students use the `get moderation result for [TEXT]` block to check whether user-submitted text is appropriate. They build a simple input checker that displays "Pass" or "Fail" based on the moderation result.

Dependencies:
* T08.G4.01: Add else to handle the opposite case
* T21.G4.01: Choose safe and specific prompts for images


ID: T21.G7.01
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Create a reusable prompt template library
Description: Students build a CreatiCode table with columns such as `subject`, `palette`, `camera`, `lighting`, and `tone`. A loop reads each row, assembles the prompt using placeholders, calls DALL-E, and records the returned costume name + URL. This ensures a whole level or comic chapter shares the same art direction.

Dependencies:
* T07.G5.01: Use a counted repeat loop
* T09.G5.04: Trace code with variables to predict outcomes

ID: T21.G7.02
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Use ChatGPT to expand briefs before generating art
Description: Students combine the `OpenAI ChatGPT: request` block (with system message + role prompt) with DALL-E. ChatGPT converts a story outline into polished prompts (e.g., "Scene 3: aerial view of neon market, magenta lighting"), then each prompt feeds the image block. Students compare raw vs. AI-enhanced prompts to see the quality improvement.

Dependencies:
* T08.G5.01: Use a simple if in a script

ID: T21.G7.03
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Audit AI imagery for representation and bias
Description: Students design experiments (e.g., run "a scientist giving a talk" 10 times) and log characteristics (perceived gender, culture, age) into a table. They graph the distribution, identify gaps, and adjust prompts (adding descriptors, requesting diversity) to reach targeted representation goals, highlighting AI4K12's focus on societal impact.

Dependencies:

Description: Students import AI-generated poses for a character, then fix artifacts (hands, faces, edges) using the costume editor or vector tools. They align all frames with equal sizing and anchor points, then script a timed animation that matches UI state (buttons, HUD cues).

ID: T21.G7.05
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Pair AI visuals with AI narration for immersive scenes
Description: Students start with a lore snippet, feed it to ChatGPT to craft narration, use `OpenAI DALL-E: generate costume image` for visuals, and convert narration to speech via `say [TEXT] in [LANGUAGE]` block. They align cues so that the voiceover references what is on screen, reinforcing cross-modal coherence.

ID: T21.G8.01
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Build a user-facing generative art widget with guardrails
Description: Students design an in-app panel (text field, preset buttons, preview box) where users can request a fresh background. The script moderates the prompt with `get moderation result`, applies house style presets, runs DALL-E, and falls back to curated art if moderation fails. Users can save approved scenes to a gallery.

Dependencies:
* T06.G6.01: Trace event execution paths in a multi‑event program
* T08.G6.01: Use conditionals to control simulation steps
* T09.G6.01: Use variables to represent real‑world quantities

ID: T21.G8.02
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Implement an approval pipeline for AI assets
Description: Students build a dashboard that lists each generated asset with metadata: prompt, author, moderation result, reviewer notes, and publish toggle. Only assets with "Approved" checked become visible in the live scene. This mirrors professional workflows and enforces accountability.

Dependencies:
* T08.G6.01: Use conditionals to control simulation steps
* T09.G6.01: Use variables to represent real‑world quantities
* T10.G6.01: Sort a table by a column
* T21.G6.06: Check user input with AI content moderation
* T21.G7.01: Create a reusable prompt template library


ID: T21.G8.03
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Produce a multi-modal media kit from one creative brief
Description: Students receive a short creative brief (setting, emotional arc). They instruct ChatGPT to output scene-by-scene descriptions, DALL-E to produce matching art, and `say [TEXT] in [LANGUAGE]` to narrate each beat. They integrate everything into a multi-screen experience where UI widgets trigger synchronized visuals + audio.

Dependencies:
* T06.G6.01: Trace event execution paths in a multi‑event program

ID: T21.G8.04
Topic: T21 – AI Media
Skill: Develop ethical guidelines for AI media use in a studio
Description: Students research a real example (e.g., a game studio using AI concept art), identify stakeholder concerns (artists, players, communities referenced), and draft a policy describing disclosure, credit, data sourcing, and escalation paths. They tie recommendations to in-class workflows (moderation logs, approvals) to show accountability.

Dependencies:
